    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer8017575417883898074">The Victorian language of flowers was used to convey romantic expressions: honeysuckle for devotion, asters for patience, and red roses for love. But for Victoria Jones, it’s been more useful in communicating mistrust and solitude. After a childhood spent in the foster-care system, she is unable to get close to anybody, and her only connection to the world is through flowe</span>
  <span id="freeText8017575417883898074" style="display:none">The Victorian language of flowers was used to convey romantic expressions: honeysuckle for devotion, asters for patience, and red roses for love. But for Victoria Jones, it’s been more useful in communicating mistrust and solitude. After a childhood spent in the foster-care system, she is unable to get close to anybody, and her only connection to the world is through flowers and their meanings. Now eighteen and emancipated from the system with nowhere to go, Victoria realizes she has a gift for helping others through the flowers she chooses for them. But an unexpected encounter with a mysterious stranger has her questioning what’s been missing in her life. And when she’s forced to confront a painful secret from her past, she must decide whether it’s worth risking everything for a second chance at happiness.<br /><b> </b><br /> Look for special features inside. Join the Circle for author chats and more.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8017575417883898074" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

<div class='communityQuestionAndAnswer'>
<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/350254-do-you-think-this-is-a-book-to-introduce">Do you think this is a book to introduce into high school curriculum? Not so much for literature purposes but to teach teenagers that they are worthy of love and forgiveness.</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_350254'><a id="like_count_community_question_350254" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/350254?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">21 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F10032672-the-language-of-flowers">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/350254-do-you-think-this-is-a-book-to-introduce">5 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/350254-do-you-think-this-is-a-book-to-introduce">See all 5 answers</a>
</li>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/4627600-lisa-maxwell"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1390483501i/4627600._UX100_CR0,24,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/4627600-lisa-maxwell">Lisa Maxwell</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">My opinion, as the mom of two young twenty-something men, is that I wouldn't have wanted them to learn about "love and forgiveness" from this book. It<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">My opinion, as the mom of two young twenty-something men, is that I wouldn't have wanted them to learn about "love and forgiveness" from this book. It sets up the YA reader for an unrealistic expectation. The heroine, Victoria, is rewarded for her churlish, anti-social behavior by a too-good-to-be-true cast of supporting characters who treat her with a God-like agape-type of love that is rarely found in this world. She is continually the beneficiary of others' generosity without ever giving back; and she never acknowledges the gifts that others have given her, never thanks them. She is a "taker" throughout, and she cuts and runs too often. As a mom, I don't see that as a constructive lesson for teens. As chick-lit and book club fodder, it's a good read. For YA readers, not so much, IMO.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>    </div>

<div id="review_143703884" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/143703884" />
    <a title="oliviasbooks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2843533-oliviasbooks"><img alt="oliviasbooks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1257619306p2/2843533.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/143703884?book_show_action=true">Jan 26, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="oliviasbooks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="oliviasbooks" href="/user/show/2843533-oliviasbooks">oliviasbooks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780345525567" href="/book/show/11514647-the-language-of-flowers">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">those who liked &quot;Raw Blue&quot; by Kirsty Eagar</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to oliviasbooks by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/3842653-nomes">Nomes</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=e-version">e-version</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=adult-fiction">adult-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=family-grief-or-other-disasters">family-grief-or-other-disasters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=contemporary-fiction">contemporary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=debut">debut</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer143703884" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3251168930225038135">The elegantly worded <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10032672.The_Language_of_Flowers' title='The Language of Flowers by Vanessa Diffenbaugh' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Language of Flowers</a> made me invest quite a lot during the first chapters, but gambled all my affection away later on. I will try to explain how this unceremonious drop around the middle of the story came to pass after introducing Victoria to you. <br/><br/>There is nothing victorious about Victoria apart from the fact that she survived to see her eighteen's birthday. Even social worker Meredith sees her only as a failure she personally doesn't deserve. A dark blotch on her white s</span>
  <span id="freeText3251168930225038135" style="display:none">The elegantly worded <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10032672.The_Language_of_Flowers" title="The Language of Flowers by Vanessa Diffenbaugh" rel="nofollow noopener">The Language of Flowers</a> made me invest quite a lot during the first chapters, but gambled all my affection away later on. I will try to explain how this unceremonious drop around the middle of the story came to pass after introducing Victoria to you. <br /><br />There is nothing victorious about Victoria apart from the fact that she survived to see her eighteen's birthday. Even social worker Meredith sees her only as a failure she personally doesn't deserve. A dark blotch on her white sheet of professional accomplishments: For Victoria has been a foundling baby, abandoned at an age that usually makes finding families willing to adopt an easy task. But somehow Victoria left and was made to leave foster family after foster family, fought in between for affection, food and physical integrity among cruel or indifferent caretakers and fellow foster kids as emotionally messed up and adapted to the loveless situations of their short lives as herself, botched up her last and only chance at a permanent solution at the age of eleven, drove Meredith crazy for the remaining seven years by countless court trials and group home fights and now, on her eighteen's birthday, the day the State of California finally rids itself from the responsibily of its parentless ward's well-being, she does not react as frightened and subdued as Meredith wished her to. On the contrary: She does not use her final three months time in the transition home to hunt for a job and find a room. She spends her days stealing flowers from communal flower beds and people's gardens to plant them in milk cartons, unconcerned about flooding and molding the carpet. On the day of her eviction into unassisted adulthood Victoria takes her flowers and moves into the concealed shrubbery of the town's recreactional area. Hunger and cold do not drive her into wanting to change her homeless lifestyle, but fear of physical abuse does, when drunk men invade her fragile sanctuary at night. Though paperless she persuades an overworked Russian florist Renata to take her on as a weekend assistant by demonstrationg her astonishing knowledge about flowers and her extraordinary skill at creating bouquets. So far so good.<br /><br />Now you would think you will see the friendship between Victoria and her new boss grow and grow and grow, some relapses to occur, love to enter her life in small, hesitant steps … Yes, I agree, that would maybe mean walking the edge of tear-jerker-like soppy, drenched in the sickly smell of forget-me-nots and red roses. But I did not expect the story to rely so heavily on flashbacks to Victoria's time on Elizabeth's vine-yard - which triggered her all-consuming obsession about the meaning each decorative plant used to have in European culture – that climax in revealing the outrageous reason for the planned adoption to go amiss <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Her actions made me really irrevocably hate Elizabeth. That was inexcusable to do to someone who felt loved and wanted for the very first time <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and for Victoria to go finally - and understandably - feral. <br /><br />My initially strong connection to Victoria slowly began to unravel, when she starts to get to know / date Grant, a young flower-farm owner she fleetingly knows from her childhood. I understood her reserve, her mistrust, her outstretched feelers. But I resented her self-centered, cat-and-mouse-style behavior <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ and it really failed me how she first sleeps under Grant's kitchen table to protect herself from him and has him sleep outside the house while she locks all doors, but suddenly decides to let him use her body without really wanting him and without spending even half a thought on contraception. There must have been dozens of pregnant or infected girls in the foster homes to observe. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. A friend of mine said Diffenbaugh's style reminded him a lot of the novels by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/566874.Sarah_Addison_Allen" title="Sarah Addison Allen" rel="nofollow noopener">Sarah Addison Allen</a>. I do understand, because the works of both contain dark pasts and the woven-in magic of fruits or flowers or gardens. My association goes into a different direction, though: The heroine Victoria and her actions reminded me the most of is Carly from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6989576.Raw_Blue" title="Raw Blue by Kirsty Eagar" rel="nofollow noopener">Raw Blue</a> by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3119823.Kirsty_Eagar" title="Kirsty Eagar" rel="nofollow noopener">Kirsty Eagar</a>. If you liked the romance in that novel, you might enjoy Victoria's and Grant's love-story as well. <br /><br />The last thread between Victoria and me was torn when she declines everyone's help <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ during her pregnancy and especially after the birth of her daughter <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, but selfishly makes the persons around her maintain, support, sacrifice, worry, plan and work for her even more than if she had accepted being advised and assisted right in the beginning. Why does she stop working? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Why does she move back into the forest during her pregnancy, depriving her unborn kid of warmth, vitamins and proper nourishment needed to thrive inside her womb? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> She could have managed. And why does she start her own and <i>illegal</i> wedding flowers business – a bitter competition to her boss' business when she could have just asked Renata to integrate her unique service into her shop's palette for a more generous salary? Since she was still using Renata's wholesale card to buy the flowers she needed, Renata could have easily done her in by simply reporting her to the authorities. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Plus, I hated the exclusiveness, that garantees her only successful mouth-to-mouth propaganda: She decides only to carter to couples who look like they will stay together, which later could be attributed to Victoria's choice of flowery accessories. The bouquets themselves are prepared by homeless girls, because only the flowers' happiness-inducing magic will be important for the wedding. How the bridal centerpiece looked and smelled and lasted, is of no concern whatsoever. A highly unlikely concept in my opinion. I, personally, would never, ever use Victoria's "Message" service. If I wanted, I could look up any flower's meaning by myself and I would not pay attrocious prices to have clumsily gathered mosses and leaves on my dinner table. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />I need to stress that I actually <i>have</i> thought maybe it's me, maybe I have just not enough stomach lining and empathy for the broken mind of someone with a devastating childhood. The author information at the end of the book mentions that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4537214.Vanessa_Diffenbaugh" title="Vanessa Diffenbaugh" rel="nofollow noopener">Vanessa Diffenbaugh</a> has personal first-hand experience with raising foster kids. Apparently she gave home to one or more. After reading the book I do not question that at all. But when I compare my reading experience of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10032672.The_Language_of_Flowers" title="The Language of Flowers by Vanessa Diffenbaugh" rel="nofollow noopener">The Language of Flowers</a> to that of other stories featuring difficult or hard-to-like main characters, I am sure that a truely skillful author can make me feel and ache and root for <i>any </i> protagonist, no matter how strange or evil. I have just finished reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10165727.Froi_of_the_Exiles__Lumatere_Chronicles___2_" title="Froi of the Exiles (Lumatere Chronicles, #2) by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Froi of the Exiles</a> (yes, it is Fantasy, I know). Fact is, when I was reading the volume preceeding it, I would have <i>never</i> guessed <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/47104.Melina_Marchetta" title="Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Melina Marchetta</a> would get me to like him. Now I love him <i>fiercely</i>. <i>Maybe</i> his personal growth is fantastical, unrealistic, but <i>maybe</i> it is simply magic. The kind of magic only the best authors can evoke in a reader's mind. <br /><br />Because of that believe I do not feel any reservations to rate the second half of this book only with two stars in contrast to my four star expectation in the beginning.<br /><br />Completely off-track, but on my mind: If you like flower-shop-based plots, you might perhaps enjoy the Japanese movie <a href="http://www.dramacrazy.net/japanese-movie/oto-na-ri/" rel="nofollow noopener">Oto-na-ri</a>. It is about a lonely thirty-something florist and a celebrity photographer, who dreams of shooting Canadian landscapes, living wall-to-wall in an apartment building without meeting each other. It is sad and funny and bittersweet. I loved it.<br /><br />A lot of thanks go to Netgalley and to the publisher, Random House, for giving me access to an electronic review copy in exchange for this honest review. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3251168930225038135" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_227320546" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/227320546" />
    <a title="kari" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2207055-kari"><img alt="kari" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1262446392p2/2207055.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/227320546?book_show_action=true">Oct 25, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="kari" class="user" itemprop="url" name="kari" href="/user/show/2207055-kari">kari</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2207055-kari?shelf=2011">2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer227320546&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer227320546" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3543397976914231258">Too much folding! “He folded himself into a chair. She folded her feet beneath her. He folded over in exhaustion placing his head on the table. She folded over in pain. She folded herself underneath the bush.” <br/>How about: “He sat in a chair. She pulled her feet beneath her. He slumped over in exhaustion. She bent over in pain. She curled herself underneath the bush.”<br/>Really, another verb is needed here and fold/ed was most overused. Yes, I am nitpicking, but since I was bothered enough to comment,</span>
  <span id="freeText3543397976914231258" style="display:none">Too much folding! “He folded himself into a chair. She folded her feet beneath her. He folded over in exhaustion placing his head on the table. She folded over in pain. She folded herself underneath the bush.” <br />How about: “He sat in a chair. She pulled her feet beneath her. He slumped over in exhaustion. She bent over in pain. She curled herself underneath the bush.”<br />Really, another verb is needed here and fold/ed was most overused. Yes, I am nitpicking, but since I was bothered enough to comment, the overuse of it was noticeable and bothersome. <br /><br /><i>Synopsis:<br />Foster child ages out of the system, plants a garden in a city park, sleeps under a bush.<br />Meets a florist who gives her a job, meets a man, rents a tiny blue room.<br />Gets pregnant, runs away to sleep under the bush.<br />Has baby, runs away to sleep under the bush.<br />Give baby away.<br />Happy ending.</i><br /><br />The problems I have with this are that there isn’t any reason for any of the people who help this girl to want to help her. She snarls and sulks and is so hard and distant that I was left wondering why any of these people wanted to be around her let alone assist her. No one knows her sad/bitter/hostile history and she isn't talking so why should they feel anything for her? <br />It didn’t appear that under all her anger that there was a gentle caring person. She seems more that if you scratched the surface, first of all, you’d definitely get scratched back, but that under that tough exterior, you’d find something even harder and more unyielding. Can’t say that I liked Victoria much. <br />So can you enjoy a book when you don’t really like the protagonist? I find it can be difficult, but in the hands of a crafted writer, you can still enjoy the story. I didn’t find that to be true here. <br />For me, the story would have been better told in third person. I think some distance between Victoria’s mean thought process and the reader would have helped. I didn’t much like being in this misanthropic head and I didn’t get any idea of anyone else’s motivation for caring for her. Why did Renata hire her? Yes, she’s a magical flower genius, but why would she want this girl around, glaring at her customers? Yes, lots of glaring.<br />And Grant, why is he attracted to her? Does he have a thing for mean women? More snarling and glaring. He seems like a very gentle soul to be that way, didn’t understand what he saw in her, other than her ability to send messages by flowers.<br />Victoria’s negativity was so over the top. She finds out she’s pregnant and hates the idea of a baby, but won’t get an abortion because the idea that someone else would have control over her body for the time it would take to get the thing out (that’s how she thinks of it) is too horrid for her to think about. She is offered medical benefits by her employer, but instead she runs away to live under a bush. No, I am most certainly not kidding. <br />Having decided to have the baby and afterward figure out what she’s going to do with it, she gets no prenatal care, not even bothering so little as to pick up a bottle of prenatal vitamins at the drugstore. No, she’s too busy hiding under the bush. <br />And she spent hours in the library comparing flower meaning dictionaries(and countless hours photographing flowers with old time camera which she spends money on the film development even though she has very little money), but didn't bother to read one single book on pregnancy or child care. <br />So, again, not that first doctor visit and she knows a midwife, willing and ready to help her, but she doesn’t want that either. She’s going to give birth at home, alone, all by herself, because ... I have no idea what is wrong with her at this point. <br />Many people have shown her that they care about her, that they’re willing to help her, but she can’t accept it. I get that we’re supposed to believe that she’s so broken(she was an abandoned baby who never found a real forever home) that she sees herself as unworthy of anyone’s concern, but how it came off to this reader is that she’s too selfish and stubborn to do what’s right. This is when my connection to her broke down completely.<br />Also, after hiding in the bush, she comes back, continuing to hide while also building herself an amazing floral designing business. Uh-huh. I believe my suspension of disbelief was at the breaking point by this time.<br />Well, what a surprise, she isn’t able to have the baby all by herself so she gets help and after a week(during which she doesn't bother to even name the child), she gives it away (not for adoption), even though she could have asked for help, could have at the very least told someone when that person is there, in the room with her, asking her how she’s doing, that she wasn’t doing well. But no, she cannot do that. I have no idea why. And no one, not one single person, asks her where her child went. Not one. Did she bury it in her garden in the park? Toss it in the ocean? Where is it? <br />I know this is fiction, but that can't excuse complete disregard for life as it is or common sense. It's based in the real world. If a woman had a child she didn't want and that child disappeared a week later, that woman is going to be getting a serious visit from the police. Yet, she comes back without the child, glares all round, states that she won't talk about it and they all accept it. Really? REALLY?<br />I can’t recommend this one. Too irritating in style, characterization and unlikely plot.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3543397976914231258" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_436154530" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/436154530" />
    <a title="Anne OK" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/285610-anne-ok"><img alt="Anne OK" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1505981069p2/285610.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1609182043?book_show_action=true">Mar 30, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lindsay - Traveling Sisters Book Reviews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lindsay - Traveling Sisters Book Reviews" href="/user/show/54886546-lindsay---traveling-sisters-book-reviews">Lindsay - Traveling Sisters Book Reviews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54886546-lindsay---traveling-sisters-book-reviews?shelf=2020-favourites">2020-favourites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1609182043" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10564130702526861834">5 stunning stars!<br/><br/>This book was even better than I had hoped for (and I had high hopes!)!<br/><br/>I have had this book on my shelf for years and have read countless raving reviews. To be honest, I was worried this might end up being one of the many over-hyped books I’ve been reading lately. It is not! It fully lived up to the hype (and more)!<br/><br/>Exquisitely beautiful writing. Heart wrenching storyline. Endearing and unforgettable characters. This was done to perfection.<br/><br/>Victoria is a young woman who grew up in</span>
  <span id="freeText10564130702526861834" style="display:none">5 stunning stars!<br /><br />This book was even better than I had hoped for (and I had high hopes!)!<br /><br />I have had this book on my shelf for years and have read countless raving reviews. To be honest, I was worried this might end up being one of the many over-hyped books I’ve been reading lately. It is not! It fully lived up to the hype (and more)!<br /><br />Exquisitely beautiful writing. Heart wrenching storyline. Endearing and unforgettable characters. This was done to perfection.<br /><br />Victoria is a young woman who grew up in foster care system. Emotionally damaged by the back and forth between numerous foster homes and group homes, she is unable to maintain healthy relationships. She constantly chooses self-destructing behaviour and pushes herself away from those who care. Her one true connection is to the language of flowers which is how she makes her mark in the world. Each plant and flower holds a true meaning and when placed skillfully and precisely in an arrangement, conveys deep meaning.<br /><br />I adored Victoria! She is flawed and insecure, yet strong and set in her ways. I had a deep connection with her from the first chapter and whole-heartedly enjoyed following her emotional and heart-wrenching journey. There is a strong theme of motherhood among these pages, specifically mother-daughter relationships, that will stay with me a long time. The relationships within this novel are complex and emotional. I was completely immersed within each of Victoria’s relationship, finding myself analyzing each scenario and situation the characters found themselves in. Though I did not agree with many of Victoria’s personal choices, I was committed to rooting for her to find true happiness and contentment. <br /><br />This is a beautiful book that has earned a spot on my Favourites List. It is one to be savoured and not rushed through. I highly recommend and look forward to reading more from this very talented author.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10564130702526861834" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/506367427?book_show_action=true">Jan 14, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Diane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Diane" href="/user/show/4845039-diane">Diane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer506367427" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14276924046331095672">Sorry if I post this review twice. I somehow "lost" the one I was writing.<br/><br/>This book is the darling of book clubs all over the country but I found it to be insipid and flawed. It showed great promise for about the first third. Diffenbaugh seemed to show an accurate and heartbreaking portrait of a young girl who is let down by the foster care system. She is angry and damaged. This was believable and felt very real.<br/><br/>The rest of the book didn't make a lot of sense to me. This broken young woman is sa</span>
  <span id="freeText14276924046331095672" style="display:none">Sorry if I post this review twice. I somehow "lost" the one I was writing.<br /><br />This book is the darling of book clubs all over the country but I found it to be insipid and flawed. It showed great promise for about the first third. Diffenbaugh seemed to show an accurate and heartbreaking portrait of a young girl who is let down by the foster care system. She is angry and damaged. This was believable and felt very real.<br /><br />The rest of the book didn't make a lot of sense to me. This broken young woman is saved and loved by many people as she embarks into her new life as an emancipated adult. Why? She's dirty and slow to communicate. She disappears without explanation. She isn't at all loveable.<br /><br />The author has quite a few errors in grammar (where was the editing?) and overuses some verbs. I was very tired of characters being "startled" for instance. I also felt that the use of foreshadowing was done with a very heavy hand. I didn't need to be clobbered over the head with it. A subtle hint would have been enough.<br /><br />This author shows promise but this novel is over-rated. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14276924046331095672" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText2620449191309813048" style="display:none">The Language of Flowers, Vanessa Diffenbaugh<br /><br />The Language of Flowers is the debut novel of American author Vanessa Diffenbaugh. It was published in 2011 by Ballantine Books. <br /><br />The novel follows the fraught life of a Victoria Jones, who by the age of 18, had lived in 32 foster homes, and becomes a flower arranger. The novel was inspired by a flower dictionary, a type of Victorian-era book which defines what different types of flowers mean.<br /><br />Acacia: Hidden love<br />Alaleh: Expressing love<br />Grapefruit: My frown will kill me<br />Yarrow: Healing for a broken heart<br />Violet: Think of me<br />Amin al-Dawla's turn: Compassion<br />Portulaca: Confession of love<br />Persimmon: Bury me in the beauty of nature<br />Moss: Motherly love<br />Khalang: Alone<br />Siavoshan's blood: you are trapped<br />Darwash: I overcame all obstacles<br />Clove Tree: I love you and you don't know it<br />White clover: Think of me<br />Dandelion: Simple inspiration, loyalty, happiness and honesty<br />Camelia: My destiny is not in your hands<br />Chrysanthemum The truth is, you are a great friend of mine<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز چهاردهم ماه اکتبر سال 2016 میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: زبان گلها؛ نویسنده: ونسا دیفن باخ؛ مترجم: فیروزه مهرزاد؛ تهران، نشر آموت، چاپ سوم 1395؛ در 396 ص؛ شابک: 9786003840157؛ چاپ هفتم 1397؛ موضوع: داستانهای نویسندگان امریکایی - سده 21م<br /><br />داستان دختری به نام «ویکتوریا» است، که پس از گذران دوران کودکی خویش، در پرورشگاه، نمیتواند با کسی ارتباط بگیرد، و تنها راه ارتباط او با جهان، گلها و معنی نام آنهاست؛ «ویکتوریا»، جایی برای رفتن ندارد، و در یک پارک عمومی میخوابد؛ جاییکه از گیاهان، باغ کوچکی برای خود درست کرده است؛ خیلی زود گلفروشی محلی، راز تواناییهای او را درمییابد، و ویکتوریا میفهمد، موهبت یاری رساندن به دیگران از راه گزینش گلها را دارد؛ در این میان فروشنده ای مرموز، در بازار گل، پاسخ پرسشهای ویکتوریا، و راز دردناکی از گذشته اش را میداند؛ و ...؛ <br /><br />اقاقیا: عشق پنهان<br />آلاله: بیان عشق<br />انگورفرنگی: اخمت مرا خواهد کشت<br />بومادران: درمانی برای قلب شکسته<br />بنفشه فرنگی: به من فکر کن<br />پیچ امین الدوله: مهرورزی<br />خرفه: اقرار به عشق<br />خرمالو: مرا در زیبایی طبیعت دفن کن<br />خزه: عشق مادری<br />خلنگ: تنهایی<br />خون سیاووشان: به دام افتادنت نزدیک است<br />دارواش: من از همه موانع گذشتم<br />درخت میخک: من تو را دوست دارم و تو این را نمیدانی<br />شبدر سفید: به من فکر کن<br />قاصدک: الهام ساده، وفاداری، خوشبختی و صداقت<br />کاملیا: سرنوشتم در دست تو نیست<br />گل داوودی: حقیقت، تو دوست فوق العاده من هستی<br /><br />تاریخ بهنگام رسانی 09/04/1399هجری خورشیدی؛ ا. شربیانی</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer175715484" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer11609288627030663870">"The Language of Flowers" by Vanessa Diffenbaugh<br/>I loved this book from the beginning and didn’t want it to end. I have always had a fascination with knowing the names history of flowers and plants and love finding them in natural surroundings. This book, The Language of Flowers by Vanessa Diffenbaugh, (whose name is similar to the dieffenbachia plant) had such a moving story line in telling the story of Victoria, from her abandonment at birth, through childhood abuse, to her orphanage experience</span>
  <span id="freeText11609288627030663870" style="display:none">"The Language of Flowers" by Vanessa Diffenbaugh<br />I loved this book from the beginning and didn’t want it to end. I have always had a fascination with knowing the names history of flowers and plants and love finding them in natural surroundings. This book, The Language of Flowers by Vanessa Diffenbaugh, (whose name is similar to the dieffenbachia plant) had such a moving story line in telling the story of Victoria, from her abandonment at birth, through childhood abuse, to her orphanage experiences and her difficulties in forming and maintaining relationships. Victoria’s life is portrayed with a depth of a feeling that pulls the reader into caring about this strange and sometimes difficult young woman. The story moves back and forth in time and place within the span of her life which brings greater meaning to why she behaves the way she does with people she meets. <br /><br />Victoria reminds me of several young people I have met and worked with over the years. They may be prickly but also may produce the most beautiful lives, just as some thorny plants produce soft and beautiful flowers. It is a story that can lift you up with expectation and hope, and than then bring you down and make you sad. It is a roller coaster ride of resiliency and success combined with sadness and disappointment. <br /><br />The idea of pouring over dusty and seldom read book after book in the personal pursuit of creating your own book of flowers and their meanings struck a cord with me. What a quiet and resolved drive and passion Victoria kept mentally reconnecting to her childhood to find understanding and meaning in her own life. There was a personal relationship with the flowers Victoria worked with and it was evident with all those who became involved in her world.<br />	“The flower you’re looking for is clearly the common thistle, which symbolizes misanthropy. Misanthropy means hatred or mistrust of humankind.”<br />	“Does humankind mean everybody?”<br />	“Yes,”<br />	“I thought about this. Misanthropy. No one had ever described my feelings in single word.”<br /><br />I received this as an early reviewer copy and appreciate the opportunity to have read this book. It is hard to believe that this was a debut novel and Vanessa’s own experiences as a foster mother and teacher shine through in this novel. For me this was an outstanding selection and I will be recommending this book as a book club read. I rate it as a full 5 star book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11609288627030663870" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_193821278" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/193821278" />
    <a title="Jo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2467655-jo"><img alt="Jo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596119990p2/2467655.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/193821278?book_show_action=true">Aug 03, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jo" href="/user/show/2467655-jo">Jo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer193821278" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7205935642579554656">I have received many a horrified look when I have told people that I don't like red roses. Their expression of horror only got worse when I told them I much preferred yellow roses. I was always really confused as to why which flowers I liked would cause such a strong reaction.<br/><br/>Then I read this book and found out. <br/><br/><u>Translation Time.</u><br/>"I don't like red roses" = "I don't like love".<br/>"But I love yellow roses" = "But I love infidelity".<br/><br/>o.O<br/><br/>Now, I'm guessing that this wasn't actually the reason why the look</span>
  <span id="freeText7205935642579554656" style="display:none">I have received many a horrified look when I have told people that I don't like red roses. Their expression of horror only got worse when I told them I much preferred yellow roses. I was always really confused as to why which flowers I liked would cause such a strong reaction.<br /><br />Then I read this book and found out. <br /><br /><u>Translation Time.</u><br />"I don't like red roses" = "I don't like love".<br />"But I love yellow roses" = "But I love infidelity".<br /><br />o.O<br /><br />Now, I'm guessing that this wasn't actually the reason why the looked at me in horror because...um, well, not many people know that flowers have meanings behind them never mind what they were. But I still thought it was interesting because red roses are <i>always</i> associated with romance and lurrrve.<br /><br />But anyway, that has nothing to do with this book.<br />Well, it kind of does because it just shows how unique and interesting I found it. <br /><br />[FYI: My other two favourite flowers (Orchids and lilies) mean refined beauty and majesty respectively, so that's better :)]<br /><br />Anyway, I really really loved this book. I wasn't sure at first and that's why I put it off for so long, but once I picked it up I was completely engrossed. <br />This book had a great dreamy almost magical realism feel about it. And magical realism is my favourite kind of realism. I love the characters, even when I hated them, and the writing was just glorious without being too... wait for it.... *cough* <i>flowery</i>. <br />Ms Diffenbaugh's story was perfectly constructed; with all these little layers added on and meshed together. I think I loved the 'past' chapters marginally more than I liked the "present" ones, for I adored Elizabeth. But then we have Grant.... oh Grant. ♥<br /><br /><i>"For years my message-laden flowers had been faithfully ignored, an aspect of my communication style that gave me comfort. Passion, connection, disagreement, or rejection: None of these was possible in a language that did not elicit a response. But the single sprig of mistletoe, if the give did indeed understand its meaning, changed everything."</i><br /><br /><br />*Girly sigh*<br /><br /><br />Without spoiling it too much, I really loved the ending. Victoria is a flawed character and she is not always likeable. AT ALL. But I really appreciated the ending that she was given. I think I could have gone either way, but Ms Diffenbaugh chose the right one. <br />Maybe it's just me, but I like it when books end with the beginning of a new journey. <br /><br />This review has kind of been thrown together, I apologise. This book deserves better but I thought I'd finish off by sending Ms D a little message.... of the floral kind, about my feelings about this book.<br /><br />*clears throat*<br /><br />Dear Ms Diffenbaugh,<br /><br />I present you with a trilliam to represent <i>modest beauty</i>. I was prepared for this book to lose me completely because of high-brow, literaryness, and get too tangled up in a vine-like metaphor. But it didn't. It's a very subtle and quiet book and it's wonderful. <br /><br />And I present you with some lupine which means <i>imagination</i> because wow, this premise was brilliant. I also give you a few yellow roses because, as we know, they could also represent <i>jealousy</i>. And I am jealous that I didn't come up with this story. *grumbles*<br /><br />I also present you with a purple rose, because this book had me <i>enchanted</i>. <br /><br />I also have this can of tinned pineapple (I'm sure it counts) which means <i>"You are perfect"</i>... if you could just give that to Grant for me? Thanks.<br /><br />And, nearly done, here is some raspberry. Not to make a fruit salad with the pineapple but to represent <i>remorse</i> that it took me so long to read this book.... but you can eat it if you want. <br /><br />And lastly, I present you with a poppy because this book was <i>fantastic</i>.<br /><br /><br /><i>I received a copy of this book from the publishers.</i><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7205935642579554656" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1805088175?book_show_action=true">Mar 13, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brenda - Traveling Sisters Book Reviews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brenda - Traveling Sisters Book Reviews" href="/user/show/10841164-brenda---traveling-sisters-book-reviews">Brenda - Traveling Sisters Book Reviews</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1805088175" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17158664513366896761">The Language of Flowers is a mesmerizing, unforgettable hopeful story that beautifully weaves the past and present while exploring abandonment, love and finding what triggers a person to open up to others. In the past, we see Victoria’s self-destructive ways as she grows up in foster homes. Now through her connections to flowers, she starts to open up by speaking the language of flowers to help people find some joy through flowers. Flowers start to connect Victoria to others as she tries to lear</span>
  <span id="freeText17158664513366896761" style="display:none">The Language of Flowers is a mesmerizing, unforgettable hopeful story that beautifully weaves the past and present while exploring abandonment, love and finding what triggers a person to open up to others. In the past, we see Victoria’s self-destructive ways as she grows up in foster homes. Now through her connections to flowers, she starts to open up by speaking the language of flowers to help people find some joy through flowers. Flowers start to connect Victoria to others as she tries to learn to trust herself.<br /><br />The characters are like a beautiful bouquet of flowers and Vanessa Diffenbaugh weaves a moving story here with the bonds between damage Victoria and the characters. Each brought some emotional conflict to Victoria while also bringing something heartwarming to the story. Victoria stole my heart and, left me heartbroken with her self-destructive ways. Victoria’s foster mother, Elizabeth, warmed my heart with her love, how she always saw the beauty in Victoria and her commitment to her. I rooted for each bond between the characters to bloom and fear the storms that threatened them.<br /><br />The ending wrapped up so well and left me with the most satisfying feels. Just what I needed right now. I highly recommend it.<br /><br />For more Traveling Sisters reviews can be found here<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://travelingsistersbookreviews.com">https://travelingsistersbookreviews.com</a></span>

<div id="review_1432060779" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1432060779" />
    <a title="Suzanne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11889829-suzanne"><img alt="Suzanne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593566451p2/11889829.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1432060779?book_show_action=true">Nov 02, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Suzanne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Suzanne" href="/user/show/11889829-suzanne">Suzanne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780230755062" href="/book/show/12200321-the-language-of-flowers">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11889829-suzanne?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11889829-suzanne?shelf=gift-from-goodreads-friend">gift-from-goodreads-friend</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11889829-suzanne?shelf=leant-copy-not-returned">leant-copy-not-returned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1432060779" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10572837460154822474">This book was to me, the language of growth, acceptance, and love and of coming home. I have many books on my shelf, but this one stood out simply as I remembered a quick line from a friend, saying she loved it – thanks Jools for this, and for my book.<br/><br/>This was special, and did really suit me in the form of short intense chapters, alternating between the past and present. Tethering me somewhere between constantly feeling bereft yet hopeful, but precariously edgy. I did not put this book down on m</span>
  <span id="freeText10572837460154822474" style="display:none">This book was to me, the language of growth, acceptance, and love and of coming home. I have many books on my shelf, but this one stood out simply as I remembered a quick line from a friend, saying she loved it – thanks Jools for this, and for my book.<br /><br />This was special, and did really suit me in the form of short intense chapters, alternating between the past and present. Tethering me somewhere between constantly feeling bereft yet hopeful, but precariously edgy. I did not put this book down on many occasions. <br /><br />Lovely Victoria learns the art of flowers language from a young age, and we learn about her as she starts this life lesson. It was a continual blossoming, and the floral images amazing. I am not capable of even arranging a simple arrangement, but the imagery created for me was breathtaking and evocative.<br /><br />“Even I didn’t know how I would react on any given day. About our deepening relationship, I felt fear and desire in equal, unpredictable parts. At the end of each night he walked outside to wherever it was he slept, and I locked the door behind him”. <br /><br />I want to see these blooms: “I dipped my nose into the bouquet I’d assembled. There was flax, and forget-me-not, and hazel. There were white roses and pink ones, helenium and periwinkle, primrose, and lots and lots of bellflower. Between the tightly wrapped stems I’d packed velvety moss, barely visible, and I had sprinkled the bouquet with the purple and white petals of Grant’s Mexican sage.”<br /><br />This story was almost wrapped up too neatly, but it fit so well. I hope some of you read it, it almost smells so good!<br /><br />This author has weaved such a knowledge of her craft, and I now have my own copy of ‘Victoria’s Dictionary of Flower’s’ in the back of the book. No need to google images, this is better. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10572837460154822474" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_329844281" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/329844281" />
    <a title="Aryn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6415628-aryn"><img alt="Aryn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560285805p2/6415628.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/329844281?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aryn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aryn" href="/user/show/6415628-aryn">Aryn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780345525550" href="/book/show/13581132-the-language-of-flowers">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6415628-aryn?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6415628-aryn?shelf=won-in-giveaway">won-in-giveaway</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6415628-aryn?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6415628-aryn?shelf=chick-lit">chick-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer329844281" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16556306970438686552">I received this book from Goodreads Giveaways.<br/><br/>After my recent horrendous experience with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2520383.The_Rose_Labyrinth' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Rose Labyrinth</a>, which had me wanting to claw my eyes out after four sentences, it was wonderful to come across a novel with such a graceful writing style that was apparent from the first page.<br/><blockquote>
  <i>For eight years I dreamed of fire. Trees ignited as I passed them, oceans burned. The sugary smoke settled in my hair as I slept, the scent like a cloud left on my pillow as I rose. Even so, the moment my mattres</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText16556306970438686552" style="display:none">I received this book from Goodreads Giveaways.<br /><br />After my recent horrendous experience with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2520383.The_Rose_Labyrinth" rel="nofollow noopener">The Rose Labyrinth</a>, which had me wanting to claw my eyes out after four sentences, it was wonderful to come across a novel with such a graceful writing style that was apparent from the first page.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>For eight years I dreamed of fire. Trees ignited as I passed them, oceans burned. The sugary smoke settled in my hair as I slept, the scent like a cloud left on my pillow as I rose. Even so, the moment my mattress started to burn, I bolted awake. The sharp, chemical smell was nothing like the hazy syrup of my dreams; the two were as different as Indian and Carolina jasmine, separation and attachment. They could not be confused.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />That being said, I was really torn as to whether this was a three star book or a four star one. In writing style it was a four. I really found myself sucked into it; it only took me 6 hours to read, and that in one sitting. In the plot, it was a three. The first half of the book's story was <i>very</i> good; the second half had sort of a nosedive as it became more and more predictable. In character development, it was a four. Victoria was well written and well explored. She had believable positive and negative quirks in her personality. In love interest, it was a three. Victoria is fickle and nonsensical and acts completely out of character when it comes to love and sex. I'm not sure she really truly loves him <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[but ends up with him?! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Basically, I was torn.<br /><br />It was like drinking a soda. I loved, loved, loved the beginning of the novel. It was fizzy and exciting and interesting (even though I've read a lot like it). Then somewhere is started to fall flat. The predictability stopped being endearing and the characters became more obnoxious.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16556306970438686552" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4667755262249863735">I received this book through a postal book swap and we were just permitted to post online as we are through our rotation.<br/><br/>When this book first came out, I kept seeing the hard cover everywhere with its very striking image of white blossoms and a black background. It kind of had the look of a romance novel, so I hadn't tried it. My friend Kathryn read and loved it, and that had landed it on my to-read list, but I hadn't gotten around to it. I was happy to do so when it ended up in my mail, because</span>
  <span id="freeText4667755262249863735" style="display:none">I received this book through a postal book swap and we were just permitted to post online as we are through our rotation.<br /><br />When this book first came out, I kept seeing the hard cover everywhere with its very striking image of white blossoms and a black background. It kind of had the look of a romance novel, so I hadn't tried it. My friend Kathryn read and loved it, and that had landed it on my to-read list, but I hadn't gotten around to it. I was happy to do so when it ended up in my mail, because I needed a nudge.<br /><br />This was a very readable book, and I read it all in a day when I was lounging around a resort in Orlando while my husband went to some conference sessions. It made for a very enjoyable vacation read!<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[It was hard for me to get rid of the idea that this was a romance novel. I expected the weird romance born of flower language to work out, and I did NOT anticipate her abandoning her child and sleeping in the dirt. So it took a sadder direction than I expected, but I was almost glad to see love not conquering all, at least not traditionally, and not on the first try. And I liked the realistic look at the foster care system. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Actual read date: 8 May 2017. Date listed is date review is posted.</span>

<div id="review_2238674262" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2238674262" />
    <a title="Justin Tate" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23082940-justin-tate"><img alt="Justin Tate" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593157920p2/23082940.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2238674262?book_show_action=true">Jan 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Justin Tate" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Justin Tate" href="/user/show/23082940-justin-tate">Justin Tate</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2238674262" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10966839376474082304">I’m probably not the target audience for this book, but I’m not NOT the right audience. Thematically it reminded me a lot of Kitchens of the Great Midwest which I thought was superb.<br/><br/>The writing wasn’t bad, the pacing wasn’t a slog. Maybe I just wasn’t in the mood for another orphan story. Seems like every book has an orphan in it these day. Why? Are we in the midst of a global identity crisis? Maybe it’s just one of those random trends, like every novel having “Girl” in the title nowadays.<br/><br/>Anyway</span>
  <span id="freeText10966839376474082304" style="display:none">I’m probably not the target audience for this book, but I’m not NOT the right audience. Thematically it reminded me a lot of Kitchens of the Great Midwest which I thought was superb.<br /><br />The writing wasn’t bad, the pacing wasn’t a slog. Maybe I just wasn’t in the mood for another orphan story. Seems like every book has an orphan in it these day. Why? Are we in the midst of a global identity crisis? Maybe it’s just one of those random trends, like every novel having “Girl” in the title nowadays.<br /><br />Anyway I wasn’t a fan of this one. I enjoyed being educated on the language of flowers, but felt no sympathy for the characters. I don’t need all my characters to be likable, but I don’t want them to be obnoxious and annoying. Just couldn’t end fast enough. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10966839376474082304" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Brandice" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36348070-brandice"><img alt="Brandice" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582594594p2/36348070.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1540934191?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brandice" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brandice" href="/user/show/36348070-brandice">Brandice</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1540934191" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10248924600334738693">I love flowers although my knowledge of them is fairly limited, and I really liked this story, where flowers played a central role. <br/><br/><i>The Language of Flowers</i> is a story about Victoria, now a young woman, who was recently emancipated from the court system at 18. She struggles with feelings of abandonment and low self-esteem, as a result of a series of events from her past, stemming from growing up as an orphan. She lives in San Francisco and works in a flower shop. She has no friends, limited relat</span>
  <span id="freeText10248924600334738693" style="display:none">I love flowers although my knowledge of them is fairly limited, and I really liked this story, where flowers played a central role. <br /><br /><i>The Language of Flowers</i> is a story about Victoria, now a young woman, who was recently emancipated from the court system at 18. She struggles with feelings of abandonment and low self-esteem, as a result of a series of events from her past, stemming from growing up as an orphan. She lives in San Francisco and works in a flower shop. She has no friends, limited relationships, and initially, pretty limited human interaction. Without directly stating this, it becomes clear that she’s afraid of getting close to people, for fear of hurting them as she expects she will yet again, be a disappointment. <br /><br />The book shifts between Victoria’s life in present day, described above, and her life as a child, predominately in one of her foster homes at age 9. The story easily transitions back and forth between the two time periods. In addition to the flowers themselves, Victoria’s foster mother, Elizabeth, and Elizabeth’s nephew, Grant, are also central characters in the story. <br /><br />At times I thought Victoria was intentionally dislikable, and constantly engaging in self-destructive behavior. I realized though that her abandonment issues played a big role in why she chose to do some of the things she did. Despite my dislike of Victoria for a fair portion of the book, I really enjoyed the story, although a bit darker than I was expecting. I did like the ending of the story too. <br /><br /><i>The Language of Flowers</i> has messages of family, forgiveness, and learning to know one’s self, in addition to the interpretation of flowers’ various meanings.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10248924600334738693" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1038331064?book_show_action=true">Aug 27, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1038331064" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18390107671039755203">Orphaned at a young age, Victoria has been moved to different foster homes, rebelling with angry outbursts and never in one place long enough to establish any solid relationships. At the age of 10, she is taken in by a woman who teaches her the language of flowers and what each flower means. Through these teachings, Victoria is able to start positively communicating. However, when the relationship is threatened, she reverts back to behaviour that will cost her the safe haven she has found and sh</span>
  <span id="freeText18390107671039755203" style="display:none">Orphaned at a young age, Victoria has been moved to different foster homes, rebelling with angry outbursts and never in one place long enough to establish any solid relationships. At the age of 10, she is taken in by a woman who teaches her the language of flowers and what each flower means. Through these teachings, Victoria is able to start positively communicating. However, when the relationship is threatened, she reverts back to behaviour that will cost her the safe haven she has found and she retreats back into her own cold, dark world. It is through her passion of flowers she lands a job with a florist and is reunited with her turbulent past which she has difficulty reconciling her worthiness as a daughter, lover and mother. This is a story of healing and forgiveness and the power of love that is inherent in nature. I found the meaning of flowers fascinating and how they were used during the Victorian era as a means to express one's feelings for another. Wonderful read ...an easy 4 ✮<br /></span>

<div id="review_1121181596" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1121181596" />
    <a title="Margitte" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7481492-margitte"><img alt="Margitte" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1361772481p2/7481492.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1121181596?book_show_action=true">Dec 02, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Margitte" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Margitte" href="/user/show/7481492-margitte">Margitte</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=family-sagas">family-sagas</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=american-author">american-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=american-novel">american-novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=2016-read">2016-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7481492-margitte?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1121181596" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1958116385722434530">Imagine a little baby as the seed of beautiful flower who travels from birth to fruition through orphanages, group homes, foster care and the social system of America, never falling in fertile soil to take route and thrive? But then, as destiny would have it, Victoria Jones lands on a flower and vineyard farm in California where the secrets of the Victorian Floriography of the plants is revealed to this girl who only understood the human language of rejection and unworthiness to be loved. She cl</span>
  <span id="freeText1958116385722434530" style="display:none">Imagine a little baby as the seed of beautiful flower who travels from birth to fruition through orphanages, group homes, foster care and the social system of America, never falling in fertile soil to take route and thrive? But then, as destiny would have it, Victoria Jones lands on a flower and vineyard farm in California where the secrets of the Victorian Floriography of the plants is revealed to this girl who only understood the human language of rejection and unworthiness to be loved. She claimed that she could not read or write, yet understood, and collected, books on botany which was her only real connection to the world and also the key to her psyche when she met Elizabeth on her farm. For the first time in her young life as a nine-year-old girl, Victoria's soul can be unlocked by a person who understood completely and spoke 'her' language.<br /><br />Through the language of flowers she reconnects to the world, learns to trust and forgive. The language of flowers was the only language she could trust. The one way of communication she could be totally honest in. As time passes and she becomes a young adult, she learns to write her own floral dictionary in which she re-evaluated the different flowers. She basically changed the destiny of the flowers by changing their meanings. But to get to that point, she had to first lash out and destroy, the only way she learnt how to cope with her world. A long road of redemption and forgiveness was her destiny.<br /><br />Victoria was not a likable young girl and she did unforgivable harm to people, which she also had to forgive herself for. The word 'hate' came easily to her, but it would take a wise woman to teach her that hate can be passionate, disengaged, dislike, but also fear. Elizabeth taught her that her behavior was a choice, not who she was. <br /><br />I was surprised by this book. It was so much different from what I expected and well worth the read. Of course I never believed in floriography since it resembled the human impulse to box everything up without consideration of the unfairness of the action. For instance, how cruel can it be to attribute 'Hate' to the cactus plant? Or 'Deceit' and 'Materialism' to the sunflower? I have been involved in botany throughout my adult life and revel in the beauty and magic of all plants. Floriography in all its splendor was never part of it and won't be in the future. I simply regard it as a waste of time. <br /><br />However, planning the story around this theme was an unusual and perhaps ambitious undertaking which informed and entertained. Victoria's struggle to make it through a hostile world was very realistic and captivating. The author managed to mix fantasy and reality in equal measures without losing the plot or the intent. The latter being to capture the life and soul of a little girl lost in in a grown-up world where everybody else decided her destiny until she could finally make that decision herself. She rooted and blossomed. She learnt the language of love in all its different manifestations. However, for her rebirth she had to go through the pain of being born again.<br /><br />RECOMMENDED!<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1958116385722434530" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
